class="docItemContainer_c0TR"><article><nav class="theme-doc-breadcrumbs breadcrumbsContainer_Z_bl" aria-label="Breadcrumbs"><ul class="breadcrumbs"><li class="breadcrumbs__item"><a class="breadcrumbs__link" href="/weaviate/api"><span>APIs</span></a></li><li class="breadcrumbs__item"><a class="breadcrumbs__link" href="/weaviate/api/graphql"><span>Search API - theme-doc-toc-mobile tocMobile_ITEo"><button type="button" class="clean-btn tocCollapsibleButton_TO0P">On this page</button></div><div class="theme-doc-markdown markdown"><header><h1>Additional operators</h1></header>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="syntax">Syntax<a href="#syntax" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Syntax" title="Direct link to Syntax" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>Functions such as <code>limit</code>, <code>autocut</code>, and <code>sort</code> modify queries at the class level.</p>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="limit-argument">Limit argument<a href="#limit-argument" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Limit argument" title="Direct link to Limit argument" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>The <code>limit</code> argument restricts the number of results. These functions support <code>limit</code>:</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><code>Get</code></li>
<li class=""><code>Explore</code></li>
<li class=""><code>Aggregate</code></li>
</ul>

</span><span class="token string" style="color:#e3116c">&quot;Google Stadia Reviewed \u2013 Against The Stream&quot;</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">        </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">,</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">        </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">{</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">          </span><span class="token property" </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">      </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">]</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">    </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">  </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain"></span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><br></span></code></pre></div></div></div></div></details>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="pagination-with-offset">Pagination with <code>offset</code><a href="#pagination-with-offset" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to pagination-with-offset" title="Direct link to pagination-with-offset" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>To return sets of results, &quot;pages&quot;, use <code>offset</code> and <code>limit</code> together to specify a sub-set of the query response.</p>
<p>For example, to list the first ten results, set <code>limit: 10</code> and <code>offset: 0</code>. To display the next ten results, set <code>offset: 10</code>. To continue iterating over the results, increase the offset again. For more details, see <a class="" href="/weaviate/api/graphql/additional-operators#performance-considerations">performance considerations</a></p>
<p>The <code>Get</code> and <code>Explore</code> functions support <code>offset</code>.</p>

style="color:#e3116c">&quot;Playing College Football In Madden&quot;</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">        </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">,</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">        </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">{</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">          </span><span class="token property" style="color:#36acaa">&quot;title&quot;</span><span class="token operator" style="color:#393A34">:</span><span class="token plain"> </span><span class="token string" style="color:#e3116c">&quot;The 50 best albums of 2019, No 3: Billie Eilish \u2013 When We All Fall Asleep, Where Do We Go?&quot;</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">        </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">      </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">]</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">    </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain">  </span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><span class="token plain"></span><br></span><span class="token-line" style="color:#393A34"><span class="token plain"></span><span class="token punctuation" style="color:#393A34">}</span><br></span></code></pre></div></div></div></div></details>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="performance-considerations">Performance considerations<a href="#performance-considerations" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Performance considerations" title="Direct link to Performance considerations" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>Pagination is not a cursor-based implementation. This has the following implications:</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><strong>Response time and system load increase as the number of pages grows</strong>. As the offset grows, each additional page request requires a new, larger call against your collection. For example, if your <code>offset</code> and <code>limit</code> specify results from 21-30, Weaviate retrieves 30 objects and drops the first 20. On the next call, Weaviate retrieves 40 objects and drops the first 30.</li>
<li class=""><strong>Resource requirements are amplified in multi-shard configurations.</strong> Each shard retrieves a full list of objects. Each shard also drops the objects before the offset. If you have 10 shards configured and ask for results 91-100, Weaviate retrieves 1000 objects (100 per shard) and drops 990 of them.</li>
<li class=""><strong>The number of objects you can retrieve is limited</strong>. A single query returns up to <code>QUERY_MAXIMUM_RESULTS</code>. If the sum of <code>offset</code> and <code>limit</code> exceeds <code>QUERY_MAXIMUM_RESULTS</code>, Weaviate returns an error. To change the limit, edit the <code>QUERY_MAXIMUM_RESULTS</code> environment variable. If you increase <code>QUERY_MAXIMUM_RESULTS</code>, use the lowest value possible to avoid performance problems.</li>
<li class=""><strong>Pagination is not stateful</strong>. If the database state changes between calls, your pages might miss results. An insertion or a deletion will change the object count. An update could change object order. However, if there are no writes the overall results set is the same if you retrieve a large single page or many smaller ones.</li>
</ul>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="autocut">Autocut<a href="#autocut" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Autocut" title="Direct link to Autocut" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>The autocut function limits results based on discontinuities in the result set. Specifically, autocut looks for discontinuities, or jumps, in result metrics such as vector distance or search score.</p>
<p>To use autocut, specify how many jumps there should be in your query. The query stops returning results after the specified number of jumps.</p>
<p>For example, consider a <code>nearText</code> search that returns objects with these distance values:</p>
<p><code>[0.1899, 0.1901, 0.191, 0.21, 0.215, 0.23]</code>.</p>
<p>Autocut returns the following:</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><code>autocut: 1</code>: <code>[0.1899, 0.1901, 0.191]</code></li>
<li class=""><code>autocut: 2</code>:  <code>[0.1899, 0.1901, 0.191, 0.21, 0.215]</code></li>
<li class=""><code>autocut: 3</code>:  <code>[0.1899, 0.1901, 0.191, 0.21, 0.215, 0.23]</code></li>
</ul>
<p>Autocut works with these functions:</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><code>nearXXX</code></li>
<li class=""><code>bm25</code></li>
<li class=""><code>hybrid</code></li>
</ul>
<p>To use autocut with the <code>hybrid</code> search, specify the <code>relativeScoreFusion</code> ranking method.</p>
<p>Autocut is disabled by default. To explicitly disable autocut, set the number of jumps to <code>0</code> or a negative value.</p>
<p>If autocut is combined with the limit filter, autocut only considers the first objects returned up to the value of <code>limit</code>.</p>
<p>Sample client code:</p>

<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="cursor-with-after">Cursor with <code>after</code><a href="#cursor-with-after" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to cursor-with-after" title="Direct link to cursor-with-after" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>Starting with version <code>v1.18</code>, you can use <code>after</code> to retrieve objects sequentially. For example, you can use <code>after</code> to retrieve a complete set of objects from a collection.</p>
<p><code>after</code> creates a cursor that is compatible with single shard and multi-shard configurations.</p>
<p>The <code>after</code> function relies on object ids, and thus it only works with list queries. <code>after</code> is not compatible with <code>where</code>, <code>near&lt;Media&gt;</code>, <code>bm25</code>, <code>hybrid</code>, or similar searches, or in combination with filters. For those use cases, use pagination with <code>offset</code> and <code>limit</code>.</p>

<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="sorting">Sorting<a href="#sorting" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Sorting" title="Direct link to Sorting" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>You can sort results by any primitive property, such as <code>text</code>, <code>number</code>, or <code>int</code>.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="sorting-considerations">Sorting considerations<a href="#sorting-considerations" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Sorting considerations" title="Direct link to Sorting considerations" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>Sorting can be applied when fetching objects, but it&#x27;s <strong>unavailable when using search operators</strong>. Search operators donâ€™t support sorting because they automatically rank results according to factors such as <a class="" href="/weaviate/api/graphql/search-operators#vector-search-operators"><code>certainty</code> or <code>distance</code></a>, which reflect the relevance of each result.</p>
<p>Weaviate&#x27;s sorting implementation does not lead to massive memory spikes. Weaviate does not load all object properties into memory; only the property values being sorted are kept in memory.</p>
<p>Weaviate does not use any sorting-specific data structures on disk. When objects are sorted, Weaviate identifies the object and extracts the relevant properties. This works reasonably well for small scales (100s of thousand or millions of objects). It is expensive if you sort large lists of objects (100s of millions, billions). In the future, Weaviate may add a column-oriented storage mechanism to overcome this performance limitation.</p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="sort-order">Sort order<a href="#sort-order" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Sort order" title="Direct link to Sort order" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="boolean-values">boolean values<a href="#boolean-values" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to boolean values" title="Direct link to boolean values" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<p><code>false</code> is considered smaller than <code>true</code>. <code>false</code> comes before <code>true</code> in ascending order and after <code>true</code> in descending order.</p>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="null-values">null values<a href="#null-values" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to null values" title="Direct link to null values" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<p><code>null</code> values are considered smaller than any non-<code>null</code> values. <code>null</code> values come first in ascending order and last in descending order.</p>
<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="arrays">arrays<a href="#arrays" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to arrays" title="Direct link to arrays" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<p>Arrays are compared by each element separately. Elements at the same position are compared to each other, starting from the beginning of an array. When Weaviate finds an array element in one array that is smaller than its counterpart in the second array, Weaviate considers the whole first array to be smaller than the second one.</p>
<p>Arrays are equal if they have the same length and all elements are equal. If one array is subset of another array it is considered smaller.</p>
<p>Examples:</p>
<ul>
<li class=""><code>[1, 2, 3] = [1, 2, 3]</code></li>
<li class=""><code>[1, 2, 4] &lt; [1, 3, 4]</code></li>
<li class=""><code>[2, 2] &gt; [1, 2, 3, 4]</code></li>
<li class=""><code>[1, 2, 3] &lt; [1, 2, 3, 4]</code></li>
</ul>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="sorting-api">Sorting API<a href="#sorting-api" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Sorting API" title="Direct link to Sorting API" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<p>Sorting can be performed by one or more properties. If the values for the first property are identical, Weaviate uses the second property to determine the order, and so on.</p>
<p>The sort function takes either an object, or an array of objects, that describe a property and a sort order.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Parameter</th><th>Required</th><th>Type</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>path</code></td><td>yes</td><td><code>text</code></td><td>The path to the sort field is an single element array that contains the field name. GraphQL supports specifying the field name directly.</td></tr><tr><td><code>order</code></td><td>varies by client</td><td><code>asc</code> or <code>desc</code></td><td>The sort order, ascending (default) or descending.</td></tr></tbody></table>

<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="sorting-by-multiple-properties">Sorting by multiple properties<a href="#sorting-by-multiple-properties" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Sorting by multiple properties" title="Direct link to Sorting by multiple properties" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>

<h4 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="metadata-properties">Metadata properties<a href="#metadata-properties" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Metadata properties" title="Direct link to Metadata properties" translate="no">â€‹</a></h4>
<p>To sort with metadata, add an underscore to the property name.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th style="text-align:left">Property Name</th><th style="text-align:left">Sort Property  Name</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td style="text-align:left"><code>id</code></td><td style="text-align:left"><code>_id</code></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:left"><code>creationTimeUnix</code></td><td style="text-align:left"><code>_creationTimeUnix</code></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:left"><code>lastUpdateTimeUnix</code></td><td style="text-align:left"><code>_lastUpdateTimeUnix</code></td></tr></tbody></table>

<details class="details_lb9f alert alert--info details_b_Ee" data-collapsed="true"><summary>Python client v4 property names</summary><div><div class="collapsibleContent_i85q"><table><thead><tr><th style="text-align:left">Property Name</th><th style="text-align:left">Sort Property  Name</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td style="text-align:left"><code>uuid</code></td><td style="text-align:left"><code>_id</code></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:left"><code>creation_time</code></td><td style="text-align:left"><code>_creationTimeUnix</code></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:left"><code>last_update_time</code></td><td style="text-align:left"><code>_lastUpdateTimeUnix</code></td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></details>
<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="grouping">Grouping<a href="#grouping" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Grouping" title="Direct link to Grouping" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
<p>You can use a group to combine similar concepts (also known as <em>entity merging</em>). There are two ways of grouping semantically similar objects together, <code>closest</code> and <code>merge</code>. To return the closest concept, set <code>type: closest</code>. To combine similar entities into a single string, set <code>type: merge</code></p>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="variables">Variables<a href="#variables" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Variables" title="Direct link to Variables" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>
<table><thead><tr><th>Variable</th><th>Required</th><th>Type</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><code>type</code></td><td>yes</td><td><code>string</code></td><td>Either <code>closest</code> or <code>merge</code></td></tr><tr><td><code>force</code></td><td>yes</td><td><code>float</code></td><td>The force to apply for a particular movements.<br>Must be between <code>0</code> and <code>1</code>. <code>0</code> is no movement. <code>1</code> is maximum movement.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="example">Example<a href="#example" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Example" title="Direct link to Example" translate="no">â€‹</a></h3>

<h2 class="anchor anchorTargetStickyNavbar_Vzrq" id="questions-and-feedback">Questions and feedback<a href="#questions-and-feedback" class="hash-link" aria-label="Direct link to Questions and feedback" title="Direct link to Questions and feedback" translate="no">â€‹</a></h2>
